    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

He's been a legend in his own lifetime.<br/>He can remember the good old days of high adventure, when being a Hero meant one didn't have to worry about aching backs and lawyers and civilization.   <span id="freeText13837303221996165703" style="display:none">Cohen the Barbarian. He's been a legend in his own lifetime.<br />He can remember the good old days of high adventure, when being a Hero meant one didn't have to worry about aching backs and lawyers and civilization. But these days, he can't always remember just where he put his teeth...So now, with his ancient (yet still trusty) sword and new walking stick in hand, Cohen gathers a group of his old -- very old -- friends to embark on one final quest. He's going to climb the highest mountain of Discworld and meet the gods.It's time the Last Hero in the world returns what the first hero stole. Trouble is, that'll mean the end of the world, if no one stops him in time.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1945800708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17262403207425544205">Ankh-Morpork, we have an orangutan.<br/><br/>Only Terry Pratchett could parody “Houston, we have a problem” with that kind of brazen aplomb. <br/><br/>While The Last Hero, A Discworld Fable, is Pratchett’s 27th Discworld book, the real HERO here is his collaborator Paul Kidby who provides a book full of illustrations.<br/><br/>Is it me, or does Cohen look a little like Terry Pratchett?<br/><br/>Pratchett’s original Discworld illustrator Josh Kirby died in 2001, and Kidby has been drawing Rincewind and the Wizards ever since. I’m an au</span>
  <span id="freeText17262403207425544205" style="display:none">Ankh-Morpork, we have an orangutan.<br><br>Only Terry Pratchett could parody “Houston, we have a problem” with that kind of brazen aplomb. <br><br>While The Last Hero, A Discworld Fable, is Pratchett’s 27th Discworld book, the real HERO here is his collaborator Paul Kidby who provides a book full of illustrations.<br><br>Is it me, or does Cohen look a little like Terry Pratchett?<br><br>Pratchett’s original Discworld illustrator Josh Kirby died in 2001, and Kidby has been drawing Rincewind and the Wizards ever since. I’m an audiobook / eBook guy but to fully appreciate this work, a reader must get a copy of the graphic novel sized work that features pages of Kidby’s outstanding drawings that give life to the story.<br><br>Taking aim at heroes and hero worship, Pratchett describes a time when the world needs saving and Rincewind and Carrot are up for the task. Also center stage is Cohen the Barbarian and his Silver Horde as well as Blind Io and the small gods of the Discworld. Cohen and his band of octogenarian heroes invade the gates of the gods in the mystical city of Dunmanifestin. We also get to see the Discworld’s answer to Leonardo da Vinci, Leonard da Quirm.<br><br>Good fun.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450155483i/17386719._SY540_.jpg" width="304" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="17262403207425544205" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Melki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melki" href="/user/show/5293536-melki">Melki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=humorous-fiction">humorous-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer932391482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8113390119027141829"><b>'And the thing is...the <i>big</i> thing about Cohen is...he's contagious.'<br/><br/>'You mean he's a plague carrier?'<br/><br/>'It's like a mental illness, sir. Or magic. He's as crazy as a stoat, but...once they've been around him for a while, people start seeing the world the way he does. All big and simple and they want to be part of it.'</b><br/><br/>This must be how Cohen the Barbarian got his Silver Horde to follow him up the highest mountain in Discworld to return something that was stolen from the Gods. BUT - for reasons too c</span>
  <span id="freeText8113390119027141829" style="display:none"><b>'And the thing is...the <i>big</i> thing about Cohen is...he's contagious.'<br><br>'You mean he's a plague carrier?'<br><br>'It's like a mental illness, sir. Or magic. He's as crazy as a stoat, but...once they've been around him for a while, people start seeing the world the way he does. All big and simple and they want to be part of it.'</b><br><br>This must be how Cohen the Barbarian got his Silver Horde to follow him up the highest mountain in Discworld to return something that was stolen from the Gods. BUT - for reasons too complicated to go into here, it will mean the end of the world if he succeeds. So, it's up to Carrot, Rincewind and Leonard of Quirm to stop him, and...OH, YE GODS! The <s>stewardess</s> Librarian is flying the plane! <br><br><b>'Ook!' said the Librarian.<br><br>'He says we'll have to land soon,' said Carrot. 'Was there some position we're supposed to get into?'<br><br>'Ook!' said the Librarian. He seemed to be fighting the levers.<br><br>'What do you mean, "Lie on your back with your arms folded across your chest"?'</b><br><br>There's really only enough material here for a short story, Discworld Lite, if you will, but there's still plenty to enjoy. Meeting the Gods was fun. I LOVE that there is a God of Unnecessary Paperwork and a Goddess of Certain Types of Ice Cream and Short Lengths of String.<br><br>I rate the story a three. It didn't really hold my interest, though to be fair, I am ruled by the Goddess of the Easily Distracted. I found myself rushing through the text to get to more of the gorgeous artwork. <br><br>Just feast your eyes on some of these beauties:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400702021i/9710000._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="256" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400702021i/9710001.jpg" width="400" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400702021i/9710002._SY540_.jpg" width="354" height="465" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400702021i/9710003.jpg" width="365" height="416" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There you have it. A fun time, loads to look at, but a necessary read only for Discworld completists. But do borrow the book JUST to look at the pictures! Drool!</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer86915673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12658707229254295568">This was the the last book on Terry Pratchett re-read binge. <br/><br/>While not as substantial as some of the rest of his books (I'm pretty sure the wordcount is less than half of his usual) this book makes up for it by being beautifully illustrated by Paul Kidby. I've never seen an artist do such spot-on interpretations of an author's characters. Kidby's work is really amazing. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1063124251" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1063124251" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1063124251?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575081963" href="/book/show/1938308.The_Last_Hero">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1063124251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13864086325949197224">Oh, my dear Sir Terry, how you always delight me.<br/><br/>In this rather short but very good 27th volume of the <i>Discworld</i> novels, we follow Conan the Barbarian and his <s>friends</s> <s>heroes</s> horde.<br/>Conan and his troupe have been on the Disc for a VERY long time without dying. But age is a matter of perspective as anyone trying to kill them finds out very briefly before their very own meeting with Binky and his master.<br/>They've plundered, ravished and done all sorts of other things, ending up quite wealthy and ... b</span>
  <span id="freeText13864086325949197224" style="display:none">Oh, my dear Sir Terry, how you always delight me.<br><br>In this rather short but very good 27th volume of the <i>Discworld</i> novels, we follow Conan the Barbarian and his <s>friends</s> <s>heroes</s> horde.<br>Conan and his troupe have been on the Disc for a VERY long time without dying. But age is a matter of perspective as anyone trying to kill them finds out very briefly before their very own meeting with Binky and his master.<br>They've plundered, ravished and done all sorts of other things, ending up quite wealthy and ... bored.<br>So their plan is to go out on a bang. And what would be better for that than returning to the Gods what had been stolen from them by the very first hero - Conan-style though.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567098268i/28069924._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Their plan becomes known to the Patrician and he employs the wizards of Unseen University (incl. a volunteering Rincewind - yep, you read correctly), Captain Carrot, as well as his favourite naive inventor in order to stop the end of the world.<br><br>So we get a madcap ride in a very daring contraption utilizing dragons, lots of hilarity from Rincewind pointing out the obvious death traps, Gods that don't understand sarcasm and much much more. Oh, and space! Yup, this novel had everything.<br><br>This volume is also one of the special ones illustrated throughout and, I think, the very first volume Paul Kidby was the artist for (after the death of Josh Kirby). So I enjoyed both the audio version (still not as good as Nigel Planer's reading, I can't emphasize this enough) as well as my print copy (Rincewind, by the way, is depicted too young in my opinion).<br><br>A wonderful addition to the series that made me chuckle almost non-stop and even burst out laughing loudly in public places.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13864086325949197224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1935965826" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1935965826" />
    <a title="YouKneeK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek"><img alt="YouKneeK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386369592p2/25923230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1935965826?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1935965826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12632257338146867252"><i>The Last Hero</i> is the seventh book in the <i>Rincewind</i> subseries. It’s actually an illustrated novel, the first one I’ve read. It was only available as an illustrated version (unlike <i>Eric</i> which I read in a non-illustrated format), and I do think some of the illustrations were important to the story. If nothing else, the ending might not make much sense without the corresponding picture. The reader could probably guess what it showed if they’d been paying attention to the story, though.<br/><br/>The story itse</span>
  <span id="freeText12632257338146867252" style="display:none"><i>The Last Hero</i> is the seventh book in the <i>Rincewind</i> subseries. It’s actually an illustrated novel, the first one I’ve read. It was only available as an illustrated version (unlike <i>Eric</i> which I read in a non-illustrated format), and I do think some of the illustrations were important to the story. If nothing else, the ending might not make much sense without the corresponding picture. The reader could probably guess what it showed if they’d been paying attention to the story, though.<br><br>The story itself is short, but cute. Cohen and his horde of heroes are on a quest, and their heroic shenanigans might destroy the entire Discworld. A variety of familiar characters get involved in trying to prevent this and, naturally, Rincewind gets dragged into things against his will. Sort of.<br><br>I’m not a very visual person, so illustrations don’t usually do much for me. Despite that, I still enjoyed the pictures in this book. I particularly enjoyed seeing illustrations for the various characters I’ve read about over the past many books. I can’t say too many of them actually looked the way I had pictured them in my mind, but they were still fun to see. The Rincewind illustrations in particular were great. The one on the cover is funny, but not very representative of the others. The other Rincewind illustrations throughout the book all show him with this perpetual frown and a dejected look that made me laugh every time he showed up in a picture.<br><br>I don’t normally include pictures with my reviews but, seeing as how this is an <i>illustrated</i> novel, I thought it would be fun to show one of my favorite pictures in the book. :)<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489113472i/22186572._SX540_.jpg" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="12632257338146867252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Stephen Robert Collins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47521763-stephen-robert-collins"><img alt="Stephen Robert Collins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606124512p2/47521763.jpg" /></a>

  <span id="freeText15030068411302913254" style="display:none">I found this slim book tucked away behind other books. I think I hid it like a last bottle of really excellent wine. <br /><br />This time the sassy, wonderful, snide, silly, colorful, twisted thingamabobs associated with Sir Terry's wordsmithery are augmented by Paul Kidby's frantic illustrations. What a visual and verbal banquet. In my volume, page 130-131 is particularly enchanting.<br /><br />It's hard to pick a favorite character in Sir Terry's pantheon, but damn, Lord Vetinari, the cultivated, calculating, well-mannered tyrant, is ahead by a finely arched nostril.<br /><br />I read the last few pages weeping while grinning like a loon. When Sir Terry's words tickle me in all the correct places, bring on the cliche laugh and cry.<br /><br />Heroes never die. And if they do, for fucks sake don't tell them! Just feed them walrus stew and let them ride with the wind.<br /><br />Brilliant.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2908742198" />
    <a title="McKenzie/literarydragon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32853493-mckenzie-literarydragon"><img alt="McKenzie/literarydragon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479272290p2/32853493.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="McKenzie/literarydragon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="McKenzie/literarydragon" href="/user/show/32853493-mckenzie-literarydragon">McKenzie/literarydragon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575081963" href="/book/show/1938308.The_Last_Hero">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32853493-mckenzie-literarydragon?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32853493-mckenzie-literarydragon?shelf=graphic-novels-and-manga">graphic-novels-and-manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2908742198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16000874672027903092">The main word that comes to mind for this book is “cute.” It’s an adorable idea about what happens to heroes if they aren’t killed in spectacular glory when they’re young. Apparently the answer is that they go looking for adventure and not the old people kind.<br/><br/>I didn’t like the format, because the lines were really long which made it hard to read. I started holding the book a foot away from my face and it sped up the reading considerably, but it was still uncomfortable.<br/><br/>The characters are delightf</span>
  <span id="freeText16000874672027903092" style="display:none">The main word that comes to mind for this book is “cute.” It’s an adorable idea about what happens to heroes if they aren’t killed in spectacular glory when they’re young. Apparently the answer is that they go looking for adventure and not the old people kind.<br /><br />I didn’t like the format, because the lines were really long which made it hard to read. I started holding the book a foot away from my face and it sped up the reading considerably, but it was still uncomfortable.<br /><br />The characters are delightfully funny and kept me entertained when some of the plot wasn’t pulling me in as it should have. I personally found the wizard side more entertaining than the hero side. This is also the first in the series that I’ve read. I don’t think I’ll be reading more of the series partly because I think I can get as much out of them by reading only the funny paragraphs as I can by reading all three hundred pages. Also, with this book my husband read it first and...<br /><br />for the full review please visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.literarydragonreviews.website/2019/11/02/the-last-hero-by-terry-pratchett-and-illustrated-by-paul-kidby/">https://www.literarydragonreviews.web...</a></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11951948-paul?shelf=books-read-2019">books-read-2019</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer433266348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer872028987982311642">Cohen can remember many things, the time when heroes didn’t need to worry about offending people or be concerned by the ruminations of anyone in the legal industry and he wasn’t that concerned about civilisation. The thing that he was struggling to remember though, was where he’d left his teeth.<br/><br/>However, that is not the important thing, Cohen and his Silver Horde, ancient heroes from all over the Disc are on a final quest to visit the Gods. They are returning to the Gods what was stolen by the fi</span>
  <span id="freeText872028987982311642" style="display:none">Cohen can remember many things, the time when heroes didn’t need to worry about offending people or be concerned by the ruminations of anyone in the legal industry and he wasn’t that concerned about civilisation. The thing that he was struggling to remember though, was where he’d left his teeth.<br /><br />However, that is not the important thing, Cohen and his Silver Horde, ancient heroes from all over the Disc are on a final quest to visit the Gods. They are returning to the Gods what was stolen by the first hero but with added interest, with the intention of obliterating their mountain home, Cori Celesti. So that their monumental quest can be immortalised and passed into lore, they have, shall we say, persuaded a bard to come along and create the saga.<br /><br />The Wizards of the Unseen University are in a bit of a panic about this. Destroying Cori Celesti will cause the magic of Discworld to cease holding together the Disc and it will be curtain for everyone. Lord Vetinari recruits Leonard of Quirm, who sets about designing the Discworld’s second known spacecraft, The Kite. This is powered by dragons and will slingshot around the world and land in the home of the Gods. Leonard of Quirm, Captain Carrot Ironfoundersson, and a very reluctant Rincewind are to be the pilots of the craft and they are launched on their mission to say the world, except unbeknown to them, they have an extra passenger on board.<br /><br />It this to be the end of the world as they know it, or will another hero save the day?<br /><br />It has been a long while since I read a Pratchett book, and I forgot how much I love his writing. His managed to perfectly blend a carefully crafted plot, with humour, steampunk gadgets, and of course the librarian. Pratchett really was the comic fantasy master, and The Last Hero is as good as I’d expected. It is helped by the fantastic art by illustrator Paul Kidby turns the fine plot into this fantastic technicolour extravaganza.</span>

<div id="review_168812968" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168812968" />
    <a title="Toby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5454475-toby"><img alt="Toby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542247337p2/5454475.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168812968?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Toby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Toby" href="/user/show/5454475-toby">Toby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780575068858" href="/book/show/34540.The_Last_Hero">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=fantastical">fantastical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168812968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10985286873656502621">A small story, clearly germinated whilst working on the previous Disc instalment, covering the effects of time and ageing, the desire to live longer, see more, put a mark on the world you are about to leave behind. Perhaps a clear example of the authors knowledge that he was going to have his life cut short by Alzheimer's? And also using the story to kill off one of his earliest creations, leftover from the silly days when the Disc was basically a spoof of fantasy novels. Cohen the Barbarian is </span>
  <span id="freeText10985286873656502621" style="display:none">A small story, clearly germinated whilst working on the previous Disc instalment, covering the effects of time and ageing, the desire to live longer, see more, put a mark on the world you are about to leave behind. Perhaps a clear example of the authors knowledge that he was going to have his life cut short by Alzheimer's? And also using the story to kill off one of his earliest creations, leftover from the silly days when the Disc was basically a spoof of fantasy novels. Cohen the Barbarian is bored, sick of living a respectable life as the dictator who overthrew the emperor of the Agatean Empire he is off to fight the many gods on Cori Celesti, because much like Roy Batty in Blade Runner he wants more life fucker. In addition to Cohen we are once more treated to a Rincewind appearance (ugh), as he is bundled in to a spaceship alongside Captain Carrot and the inventor Leonard of Quirm, off to save the world from The Silver Horde, with assistance from Ponder Stibbons. It's a small story bringing together many of Pratchett's regular characters, it's light on substance but as the title suggests it's designed as a fable and as such there's a lot of the usual Rincewind filler that is thankfully left on the cutting room floor and that is a small mercy. The real quality of this book is the artwork of Paul Kidby, almost every page is loaded with artistic detail and often humour, and much like Pratchett's conflict between silly and smart humour, some of Kidby's work is far more subtle than others. The double page illustrations are often more than impressive and make this book worth the price of admission alone. Without them, it becomes just a throwaway short story really.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10985286873656502621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11420319883216131621"><b>9/10. </b><br/><br/><b>The pros</b>: This was a highly enjoyable book. I've been reading the Discworld series for some years now; I'm not rushing, because there isn't going to be any more, and I'd like to go as long as possible while still having new ones to read. This one was especially charming, funny and exciting, and this book is also wonderfully illustrated.<br/><br/><b> The cons</b>: This is another of those books where I don't have any specific reason for it not being the highest possible rating, it just doesn't give me that </span>
  <span id="freeText11420319883216131621" style="display:none"><b>9/10. </b><br /><br /><b>The pros</b>: This was a highly enjoyable book. I've been reading the Discworld series for some years now; I'm not rushing, because there isn't going to be any more, and I'd like to go as long as possible while still having new ones to read. This one was especially charming, funny and exciting, and this book is also wonderfully illustrated.<br /><br /><b> The cons</b>: This is another of those books where I don't have any specific reason for it not being the highest possible rating, it just doesn't give me that <i>feeling</i>, but I loved it too much to have any criticisms!<br /><br /><b>The conclusion</b>: A lovely story and beautiful art. I forget how much I love Terry's writing until I read another of his books. I'm so honoured to know that I have so many of them still to read.</span>

<div id="review_864358076" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/864358076" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575073777" href="/book/show/47992.The_Last_Hero">review of another edition</a>

            Shelves:

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=treasure-and-adventure">treasure-and-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=illustrated">illustrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=ridiculously-prolific-authors">ridiculously-prolific-authors</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer864358076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1649449461671688853">It's been a while since I've visited the Discworld. I usually try to read two or three a year, but I only managed to read one in 2019. Plus I had to track down a copy of this since my library didn't have it, and then I never got around to reading it over the summer like I was supposed to. As always, should have read it sooner. This book tickled me.<br/><br/>This is actually considered the 27th full book of the series, despite it being about half the size, really only novella length once you take the full </span>
  <span id="freeText1649449461671688853" style="display:none">It's been a while since I've visited the Discworld. I usually try to read two or three a year, but I only managed to read one in 2019. Plus I had to track down a copy of this since my library didn't have it, and then I never got around to reading it over the summer like I was supposed to. As always, should have read it sooner. This book tickled me.<br><br>This is actually considered the 27th full book of the series, despite it being about half the size, really only novella length once you take the full page illustrations into account. It's a Rincewind book, so you know basically what you're in for there, but this book also has lots of the other Wizards, and Cohen the Barbarian, and Carrot! Carrot is my favorite. The plot centers on Cohen and his Silver Horde of old geezer heroes going on one last adventure. They've grown dissatisfied with life as Emperor and his hangers-on after one of their companions died the ignominious death of choking on a cucumber, no sword anywhere to be seen. Cohen has got it into his head that he's going to reverse what that first hero did so long ago, and give fire back to the gods. This will not go as he plans, and in fact, will result in all magic on the Disc being destroyed, and thus all life as well.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585160579i/29168455._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Wizards learn of what's happening and recruit a team to get to the Hub as fast as possible and thwart the Horde's plans. This involves Discworld style space travel, in which a crew featuring Rincewind, Carrot, and Leonard da Quirm (the inventor) have to go over the edge of the disc in order to orbit around and then drop down in the middle again. Rincewind is there because he knows Cohen, but as is standard, is a wreck. Carrot is stoic. Leonard keeps inventing ridiculous things on the fly.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585160579i/29168454._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is actually one of my favorite Discworld books so far. It spoofs space travel and heroic quests and religion, but there's an undercurrent of melancholy and sadness over the ephemeral nature of life. Cohen is a ridiculous person, but he's also a tragic character, a hero at the end of his life, with no more adventures to conquer. His plotline (in which he kidnaps a bard so that said bard will write him a saga) pairs perfectly with the three space-goers, as there were several moments of sheer beauty admidst the absurdity, where Rincewind and Carrot become possible the first humans to see the Disc from space, and the elephant rises on the horizon. Paul Kidby really nailed all the illustrations.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585156126i/29168141._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Actually, let's talk about the illustrations. I wasn't sure what to expect from an illustrated Discworld book. They're often so absurd, it feels like a very hard task to try to capture the tone, which is often many things at once. But Kidby did it! His illustrations are gorgeous, first of all, especially the ones with the views from space, and involving the turtle and the four elephants. And they manage to capture the spirit of the characters, who always take themselves incredibly seriously, even as everything they are doing is patently ridiculous, and then he managed on top of that to also capture that constant feeling of sadness and anger that often permeates Pratchett's work. I had a hard time not skipping ahead while I was reading, just to look at the pictures.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585160579i/29168456.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This might not be the best place to start with Discworld, as a lot of my enjoyment came with having known these characters already, but it's definitely one you shouldn't skip if you're already a fan, and I'm glad I own my own copy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1649449461671688853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13609586175278500407" style="display:none">I have to confess to being very disappointed that the only Audible version of THE LAST HERO available seems to be an abridged version (4 hours and 24 minutes worth), unless I'm older and blinder than I thought I was. Which is also part of the reason that I really love this book so much. Cohen the Barbarian is no youngster, and he's on a final quest to climb the highest mountain in the Discworld and meet his gods. He doesn't like the way they let men grow old and die, and they should be bloody worried about that. Cohen might struggle to remember where he put his teeth these days, but he does a good line in long remembered grudges. End of the world or no end of the world.<br /><br />Madness ensues, as you'd expect, and the band of brothers (grandfathers / okay probably g-g-g-grandfathers to be honest) that make up his "crew" have still got it, or they did have if they could remember what it was, better still, if they could get their medication levels sorted out.<br /><br />Needless to say, all a bit crazy, all a bit manic and laugh out loud to boot.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_196191347" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5743748-wastrel?shelf=r-ss">r-ss</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer196191347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9293978411789715828">An installment that it's very easy to overlook: it's only a very short illustrated novel, after all. More a lengthy short story than a novel, to be honest. And when you think about the plot, the characters and so on, it's all very simple, very small, nothing all that impressive.<br/><br/>But the flip side of that is that there's no room for most of Pratchett's vices. Combine that tight focus with an author at the peak of his powers, and the result is near-perfect execution. The comic bits are very funny, </span>
  <span id="freeText9293978411789715828" style="display:none">An installment that it's very easy to overlook: it's only a very short illustrated novel, after all. More a lengthy short story than a novel, to be honest. And when you think about the plot, the characters and so on, it's all very simple, very small, nothing all that impressive.<br /><br />But the flip side of that is that there's no room for most of Pratchett's vices. Combine that tight focus with an author at the peak of his powers, and the result is near-perfect execution. The comic bits are very funny, the tragic bits are very moving, the themes are clear and powerful. The art varies from 'mediocre' through to 'exceptional'. And it feels like a big farewell to a well-loved older incarnation of the series - many themes are shared with 'Troll Bridge' and <i>Interesting Times</i>, but the story is obviously much bigger than 'Troll Bridge', and much more succesful than <i>Interesting Times</i>. You could argue that there've very little said here that Pratchett hasn't said already, and that's probably why I get a feeling of lightness from it, and why people forget about it. But I'll say again: the execution is very close to perfect. This absolutely should not be dismissed as something second-rate, except in length and complexity. It's a small, minor, easily-overlooked brilliant little gem of a book.<br /><br />My fuller review is over at <a>my blog</a>.</span>

<div id="review_440007412" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/440007412" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashish" href="/user/show/4056309-ashish">Ashish</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061040962" href="/book/show/596897.The_Last_Hero">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4056309-ashish?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4056309-ashish?shelf=humour">humour</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer440007412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer619784915795466045"><i>"So many worlds. So little time."</i><br/>In the course of the last 26 books, Pratchett gave us a brilliant cast of characters. We've watched them appear, grow, evolve, and become a part of the Discworld Universe; Cohen was the only one who was who he was, in the beginning and till the end. That's what defined him, and that's what also, I thought, made him increasingly irrelevant in a Discworld with high-speed communications, reformed and societally-assimilated monsters, the rule of law & order and, most</span>
  <span id="freeText619784915795466045" style="display:none"><i>"So many worlds. So little time."</i><br />In the course of the last 26 books, Pratchett gave us a brilliant cast of characters. We've watched them appear, grow, evolve, and become a part of the Discworld Universe; Cohen was the only one who was who he was, in the beginning and till the end. That's what defined him, and that's what also, I thought, made him increasingly irrelevant in a Discworld with high-speed communications, reformed and societally-assimilated monsters, the rule of law &amp; order and, most of all, a full map. There were no more uncharted forests, misty mountains, desolate icefields, and endless oceans. For a Hero who lived on the edge of everything, the complete civilization of the world was the end of final chapter of his life. <br />We thought there were no more surprises left. <br /><br /><b>And he proved us spectacularly wrong. </b><br /><br />I can't help but see a touch of the autobiographical in this. A sense of nostalgia for a simpler, more mysterious, and vaster world. I don't know if it's symbolic that the last great discovery - the true mapping out of the world, above and below, also happens in this book; now that there are no more mysteries, Cohen's world is finally ended - but Cohen himself continues. He takes that final step into the only place left for him. <br />He becomes Legend. <br />And the song lives on, though the singer is forgotten. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="619784915795466045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2685482661" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2685482661" />
    <a title="Chip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1916743-chip"><img alt="Chip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444485238p2/1916743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2685482661?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chip" href="/user/show/1916743-chip">Chip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1916743-chip?shelf=discworld">discworld</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2685482661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10948422802445685007">This might just be my favorite Discworld book yet; it is definitely the most fun. it had the right balance of plot points and didn't overdo the characters and storylines that frequently cause Discworld books to bog down.<br/><br/>It was full of excellent quotes and the story kept moving along. Besides, any book with this grouping of characters is one that I will likely love - and I didn't realize how much I missed <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Carrot <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br/><br/>Characters: 5*<br/>Plot: 4.9*<br/>Universe: 5*<br/><br/>And now, my favori</span>
  <span id="freeText10948422802445685007" style="display:none">This might just be my favorite Discworld book yet; it is definitely the most fun. it had the right balance of plot points and didn't overdo the characters and storylines that frequently cause Discworld books to bog down.<br /><br />It was full of excellent quotes and the story kept moving along. It doesn't make any difference.”<br /><br />"I do not think I've become old. Just more aware of where the next lavatory is. " <br /><br />"A picture had already formed in his mind's eye. Leonard had the look of someone who was confident because, so far, he'd never found reason not to be. He would step off a high building in the happy state of mind of someone who intended to deal with the problem of the ground when it presented itself.” <br /><br />“The place where the story happened was a world on the back of four elephants perched on the shell of a giant turtle. That's the advantage of space. It's big enough to hold practically anything, and so, eventually, it does.<br />People think that it is strange to have a turtle ten thousand miles long and an elephant more than two thousand miles tall, which just shows that the human brain is ill-adapted for thinking and was probably originally designed for cooling the blood. It believes mere size is amazing.<br />There's nothing amazing about size. Turtles are amazing, and elephants are quite astonishing. But the fact that there's a big turtle is far less amazing than the fact that there is a turtle anywhere.” </span>

<div id="review_2604861830" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2604861830" />
    <a title="Ric" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35905360-ric"><img alt="Ric" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583635231p2/35905360.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2604861830?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ric" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ric" href="/user/show/35905360-ric">Ric</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575081963" href="/book/show/1938308.The_Last_Hero">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35905360-ric?shelf=2019-reading-challenge">2019-reading-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2604861830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10794310915397349391">I almost rounded down from 3.5 stars, but The Last Hero was a pretty entertaining entry to the series and it had a few things going for it. I’ve always said that Rincewind is my least favorite Discworld protagonist, and the lack of Rincewind actually works in this book’s favor. It focused a lot on the characters he was with, like Leonard of Quirm, Captain Carrot, and The Librarian. It also had a pretty entertaining subplot with Cohen the Barbarian trying to destroy the gods for letting him and h</span>
  <span id="freeText10794310915397349391" style="display:none">I almost rounded down from 3.5 stars, but The Last Hero was a pretty entertaining entry to the series and it had a few things going for it. I’ve always said that Rincewind is my least favorite Discworld protagonist, and the lack of Rincewind actually works in this book’s favor. It focused a lot on the characters he was with, like Leonard of Quirm, Captain Carrot, and The Librarian. It also had a pretty entertaining subplot with Cohen the Barbarian trying to destroy the gods for letting him and his crew get old, which was fine but again, not my personal favorite character either. It always seems to me that Rincewind’s books thrive on other characters that make appearances, like the wizards. <br /><br />The thing that was so different about this book was that it was an illustrated novel, so it had normal prose but also had a bunch of illustrations to go along with the story. And those illustrations were beautiful, though I don’t necessarily think that I’d enjoy reading every Discworld book in that format. Some of the illustrations were fantastic, there was a shot of Rincewind, Leonard, Carrot, and the Librarian standing on the moon’s surface looking back at the Disc and it was amazing. There was a full page illustration of Death and the Death of Rats that I’d blow up and hang on my wall if I could. It added a different element to the story that I liked, and it helped the rating of this story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10794310915397349391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17244342483683396140" style="display:none">I NEED TO OWN THIS BOOK ASAP. It has pictures! Of old men! And dragons! <br />Even without the illustrations, I'd buy it anyway.<br /><br />The Last Hero is technically a Rincewind book but it's mainly about Cohen &amp; The Silver Horde and Leonard of Quirm, served with a side of Carrot. It also has a bunch of other people. It's glorious. I loved Vena/Mrs. McGarry - one of the reasons I love Pratchett is because he writes awesome women. I <i>like</i> that Vena doesn't do much in the realm of swashbuckling, even though we know that she's a legend. She chooses to be Mrs. McGarry. Well, mostly. (I would love to see Xena the Warrior Princess in old age, seriously.) And the minstrel is one of those characters that I'm defenseless against, ie. he's one of those sleazy/hapless ones who grow the most during the journey (in fact, he grows up to be Orpheus, haha). <br /><br />Honestly, the whole thing is just completely rewarding and emotional in a laughing-through-your-tears sort of way. AUGH. <blockquote><b>BLIND IO:</b> I feel that if we had wanted people to fly, we would have given them wings.<br /><b>OFFLER:</b> We allow broomthtickth and magic carpeth. <br /><b>BLIND IO:</b> Ah, but they're magical. Men could look <i>down</i> upon their gods! Why did you do it? <br /><b>LEONARD OF QUIRM:</b> You gave me wings when you showed me birds. I just made what I saw.</blockquote> <br /><blockquote><b>BLIND IO:</b> Tell me. Is there a god of policemen?<br /><b>CARROT:</b> No, sir. Coppers would be far too suspicious of anyone calling themselves a god of policemen to believe in one.<br /><b>BLIND IO:</b> But you are a gods-fearing man?<br /><b>CARROT:</b> What I've seen of them certainly frightens the light out of me, sir. And my commander always says, when we go about our business in the city, that when you look at the state of mankind you are forced to accept the reality of the gods.</blockquote> <br /></span>

<div id="review_1073867226" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1073867226" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9698647-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341102729p2/9698647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1073867226?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/9698647-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9698647-matt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9698647-matt?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9698647-matt?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1073867226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer208318935134744327">The Gods are on notice as the greatest heroes of the Disc are headed for their heavenly abode on a quest to return the fire stolen by the first hero, except there’s a catch. The illustrated Discworld novella <i>The Last Hero</i> is the twenty-seventh in the humorous fantasy series written by Terry Pratchett and assisted by artist Paul Kirby. And once again Pratchett follows his first protagonist Rincewind racing to save the world.<br/><br/>Cohen the Barbarian and his Silver Horde have left their imperial possess</span>
  <span id="freeText208318935134744327" style="display:none">The Gods are on notice as the greatest heroes of the Disc are headed for their heavenly abode on a quest to return the fire stolen by the first hero, except there’s a catch. The illustrated Discworld novella <i>The Last Hero</i> is the twenty-seventh in the humorous fantasy series written by Terry Pratchett and assisted by artist Paul Kirby. And once again Pratchett follows his first protagonist Rincewind racing to save the world.<br /><br />Cohen the Barbarian and his Silver Horde have left their imperial possessions on the Counterweight continent and are heading for the home of the Disc’s Gods with the gift of fire first stolen by the legendary First Hero, unfortunately the old men are planning to blow the place to smithereens which would have the unfortunate side effect of destroying the Disc. To the rescue is Leonardo da Quirm, Captain Carrot, and a reluctant Rincewind—who only joins because if he didn’t he’d find himself on the journey by some horrible twist of fate—traveling the quickest way they can get to the abode of the Gods, over the Rim and through space. This short story is given a remarkable boost with the illustrations of Paul Kirby who brings to life so many great characters from all over the Disc, as well as two new secondary characters. Yet not only do characters get a stunning portrayal but so does the geography of the Disc as well in stunning pictures that makes you just want to stop reading and stare at them to take in all the details.<br /><br />The novella itself is pretty straight forward unlike a regular Discworld novel in which little sidebars populate the narrative to humorous effect, but with <i>The Last Hero</i> the illustrations more than make up for that. While considered a part of the Rincewind series, the Disc’s worst wizard is more a tag along character in a story dominated by usually secondary characters. However for longtime fans this won’t be a problem given the story and the amazing illustrations.</span>
  <a data-text-id="208318935134744327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_48036167" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/48036167" />
    <a title="Elise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805316-elise"><img alt="Elise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1229375272p2/1805316.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/48036167?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elise" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elise" href="/user/show/1805316-elise">Elise</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48036167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4525763474915578591">I didn't really like my first couple of experiences with Terry Pratchett. The first book I tried from Discworld was "The Color of Magic." I figured I start with it because it was the first book, but I was really disappointed with it and found it unfunny. I still wanted to give Discworld another chance though because I really wanted to like Terry Pratchett. So, I read around and found out that most people found his funniest book was "Guards! Guards!" So, I decided to buy it. I found it slightly b</span>
  <span id="freeText4525763474915578591" style="display:none">I didn't really like my first couple of experiences with Terry Pratchett. The first book I tried from Discworld was "The Color of Magic." I figured I start with it because it was the first book, but I was really disappointed with it and found it unfunny. I still wanted to give Discworld another chance though because I really wanted to like Terry Pratchett. So, I read around and found out that most people found his funniest book was "Guards! Guards!" So, I decided to buy it. I found it slightly better than "The Color of Magic," but I still found it only mildly amusing and still didn't get what the big deal of why these books are so popular. So, I swore off Pratchett for a while and decided that maybe he just wasn't my cup of tea.<br /><br />Now, for whatever reason I decided I wanted to try Pratchett again. This time I picked up "The Last Hero: A Discworld Fable." I have to say that this may very well be the first Pratchett book I actually enjoyed. Perhaps it was because it had more of a plot this time, or maybe it was because it was illustrated. The art in this book is very nice. But this time my visit to the Discworld was fun and entertaining. This time I actually found it amusing. The characters were all great, especially Cohen and his Horde. They were a really funny bunch. So, I gave Terry Pratchett another chance, and I'm glad I did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4525763474915578591" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145707486" />
    <a title="Andrew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/800291-andrew"><img alt="Andrew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295167791p2/800291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145707486?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew" href="/user/show/800291-andrew">Andrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145707486" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14192058679161696573">This book is one of the two large format books from the Discworld - (the other being Eric), however it is far more lavishly illustrated - this time by Paul KIdby - as this was published at the time of John Kirbys death. The illustrations are of a totally different style and although Kirby's style will be forever connected to the early Pratchett works I think these are just as good and compliment the story perfectly. <br/>As for the story its quiet short considering the number of illustrations through</span>
  <span id="freeText14192058679161696573" style="display:none">This book is one of the two large format books from the Discworld - (the other being Eric), however it is far more lavishly illustrated - this time by Paul KIdby - as this was published at the time of John Kirbys death. The illustrations are of a totally different style and although Kirby's style will be forever connected to the early Pratchett works I think these are just as good and compliment the story perfectly. <br />As for the story its quiet short considering the number of illustrations throughout it - and is face paced and fun to read. The story possibly because of its length contains less of the footnote explanations (synonymous with Discworld) and just gets on with the story at hand. This was a fun read and at times a little cumbersome - it was highly enjoyable - i wont say anything about the story since like so many other characters it has an impact on the rest of the series on one shape or form and there are plenty of far better spoilers out there to give you the plotline. All in all a great book to read, </span>
  <a data-text-id="14192058679161696573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7812030804348281603">2004<br/><br/>I had nothing to say about it, although I recall not liking the pictures very much.<br/><br/>***<br/><br/>2013 April 11<br/><br/>Now that I know the characters involved, I enjoyed this one enormously. Pratchett can be challenging to read: he eschews chapters, switches between scenes all over the place following different groups of characters, and basically, just throws the reader in the deep end. Now that I know more about all the major players, Rincewind, Cohen and the Silver Hoard, the Patrician, Carrot, Ponder, etc. i</span>
  <span id="freeText7812030804348281603" style="display:none">2004<br /><br />I had nothing to say about it, although I recall not liking the pictures very much.<br /><br />***<br /><br />2013 April 11<br /><br />Now that I know the characters involved, I enjoyed this one enormously. Pratchett can be challenging to read: he eschews chapters, switches between scenes all over the place following different groups of characters, and basically, just throws the reader in the deep end. Now that I know more about all the major players, Rincewind, Cohen and the Silver Hoard, the Patrician, Carrot, Ponder, etc. it all makes much more sense. <br /><br />So, Cohen is tired of being off heroing, and decides to take fire back to the gods, with interest. The Patrician, Vetinari, gets wind of this, and puts together a team to prevent what will be the end of Discworld. That mission just happens to look like all the Apollos rolled into one, in a ship designed and built by Leonardo.<br /><br />Fun stuff. Don't miss the portrait of Death with a kitten.<br /><br />Library copy.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2416843454" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2416843454" />
    <a title="Aphelia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82832336-aphelia"><img alt="Aphelia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528413347p2/82832336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2416843454?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aphelia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aphelia" href="/user/show/82832336-aphelia">Aphelia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82832336-aphelia?shelf=my-collection">my-collection</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82832336-aphelia?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82832336-aphelia?shelf=20for2020tbrchallenge">20for2020tbrchallenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2416843454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer765096319464580137"><b>A must have for any Terry Pratchett fan, especially one who loves the art of Paul Kidby and appreciates the Wizzard Rincewind! Also, this 2002 edition has 16 extra illustrations!</b><br/><br/>Let me start by saying that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett' title='Terry Pratchett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Terry Pratchett</a> is one of my all-time favourite authors! He wrote two illustrated collectible books for fans. The first was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64218.Eric__Discworld___9__Rincewind__4_' title='Eric (Discworld, #9; Rincewind #4) by Terry Pratchett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eric</a> (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3056700658?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>my review</a>), with artwork by original Discworld artist Josh Kirby, and this is the second. <br/><br/>In contrast to <b>Eric</b>, which is a short novella, this is a more fully realiz</span>
  <span id="freeText765096319464580137" style="display:none"><b>A must have for any Terry Pratchett fan, especially one who loves the art of Paul Kidby and appreciates the Wizzard Rincewind! Also, this 2002 edition has 16 extra illustrations!</b><br /><br />Let me start by saying that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" title="Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Pratchett</a> is one of my all-time favourite authors! He wrote two illustrated collectible books for fans. The first was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64218.Eric__Discworld___9__Rincewind__4_" title="Eric (Discworld, #9; Rincewind #4) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Eric</a> (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3056700658?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">my review</a>), with artwork by original Discworld artist Josh Kirby, and this is the second. <br /><br />In contrast to <b>Eric</b>, which is a short novella, this is a more fully realized book with a much richer storyline. Like the illustrated version of <b>Eric</b> (there are many versions, some just text), this is a gorgeous, oversize, big floppy paperback book with dazzling full-colour illustrations printed on thick, glossy paper.<br /><br />And there are so many amazing illustrations in this book, including some gorgeous art of Great A'Tuin, the Star Turtle, and the Four Elephants who hold the Disc, and Death, including the famous character study with the kitten (one of my favourites). <br /><br /><b>If you love Paul Kidby's Discworld art, this book is well worth buying for that alone - it's jam packed!</b> There are backgrounds, inserts, character studies, special story art, full pages, and some stunning full two-page spreads! It's an amazing portfolio.<br /><br />As for the story, I loved that too!<br /><br />Cohen the Barbarian has gotten old (he can never find his false teeth!) and after fighting injustice (of a special sort that aligns with The Heroic Code) all his life, he's determined not to go gently into any night, good or otherwise. He enlists the help of what's left of his decrepit and aged Silver Horde and decides to have it out with the Gods about the unfairness of mortality. To prove his point, he's going to return something that was stolen - mortal fire - in a spectacularly explosive way.<br /><br />As the gang embarks on the perilous journey to Cori Celesti (the Disc equivalent of Mount Olympus), back in Ankh Morpork, the Patrician has been alerted of Cohen's plans. Blowing up the mountain will drain all magic from the world, effectively ending it.<br /><br />The Patrician gathers the wizards from The Unseen University, including a very reluctant Rincewind (now in charge of Cruel and Unusual Geography, which is fitting since he's ran through so much of it), to find a way to stop Cohen. The Patrician also releases the brilliantly mad inventor Leonard of Quirm out of his attic to help. Leonard designs the first spacecraft - a giant wooden bird powered by swamp dragon fire - that will go over the Rim and then use the momentum to fly to the impossibly high City of the Gods, hopefully in time to prevent The End of the World.<br /><br />Only things don't exactly go as planned. Leonard, Rincewind and Captain Carrot (a steady man in any circumstance) become the first astronauts - but the Librarian, with his insatiable curiosity and sense for History In The Making, stows away onboard, skewing all the careful equations. With help from Ponder Stibbons, they regroup, with a stop at the Moon (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[which turns out to be full of strange silver dragons! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) along the way!<br /><br />Includes a wonderful cameo from Death, one of my favourite characters (that sounds strange, but fellow Discworld fans know what I mean). My only teeny, tiny quibble is that The Luggage - shown so nicely on the bottom of the cover flaps - wasn't more involved in things. I love that loyal, murderous hunk of sapient pearwood!<br /><br /><b>A delightful, hilarious and ultimately very affecting story about our need for heroes, and how they never truly die. A wonderful addition to any Discworld collection, a thoughtful gift idea for a fan, and very highly recommended!</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="765096319464580137" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('I+k6PWy2cQBYHMnGgPazLCa2jQm5npgy+K1AwgXe23VPxhTPZZNEwDGORrqEHW37xQthg4IueU6nKglGMbclzQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gJbZC4iK1+bUKTb9Fb+NY8JUpWqG7Ql+BoLfmYGJcrTsuff5ga/iJr27uYERVFO0IelJ4L1d6AJZBZYdteCMDA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">About Terry Pratchett</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1829408555862162359">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br/><br/>Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, i</span>
  <span id="freeText1829408555862162359" style="display:none">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <i>The Color of Magic</i>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <i>Good Omens</i>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <i>Nation</i>. Terry published <i>Snuff</i> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire (OBE) “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from the University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, the University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
